أي أعطى شخصاً واحداً في يوم واحد قدر الشهرين لا يجوز إلا عن هذا اليوم، هذا مذهبنا، وأما عند الشَّافِعِي فلا بُدَّ من التمليك، كما في الكسوة، ووجه قولنا: ما ذُكِرَ في أصول الفقهِ في دلالةِ النَّص: إن الإطعام جعلُ الغيرِ طاعماً، وهو بالإباحة... إلى آخره. إباحة الطعام، فإنّها لا تتجدّد في يوم واحد. وإن أطعم ستين مسكيناً كلاً صاعاً من بر عن ظهارين لم يصح إلا عن ظهار واحد، وعن إفطار وظهار صح، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وأما عند محمد فإنه يجوز عن الظهارين هما يقولان النيَّةُ تعمل عند اختلافِ الجنسين كالإفطار والظهار، لا عند اتحادِهما، فإذا لَغَت النية والصاعُ يصلح كفارة واحدة؛ لأنَّ نصفَ الصاع من أدنى المقادير، فالمؤدى وهو الصاع يصلح كفارة واحدة جَعَلَها للظهارين فلا يصح. يصير العين كفارة، وذا بتمليك العين لا بالإعارة، إذ هي ترد على المنفعة على أنَّ الإباحة في الطعام تتم المقصود دون إعارة الثوب. وفي المقام أسئلة وأجوبة مذكورة في «التلويح». قوله: وإن أطعم ... الخ؛ يعني لو كانت عليه كفارة ظهارين فأطعم ستين مسكيناً عنهما معاً بأن أعطى كلاً منهم صاعاً من حنطة، ونوى نصف صاع من ظهار ونصفه من آخر لم يجزه إلا عن واحدٍ منهما عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، وإن أطعم ذلك عن مختلفي الجنس ككفّارة إفطار رمضان، وكفارة ظهار أجزأ عنهما اتفاقاً. له: أنّ في المؤدي وفاء بالظهارين، والفقير المصروف إليه محلّ لهما، فيقع عنهما كما عنه اختلاف السبب واختلاف الفقير. ولهما: إنّ النية في الجنس الواحد لغو، وتعتبر في الجنسين، وإذا لغت النية والمؤدّي يصلح كونه لكفارة واحدة، فيقع عنها.
If he gives a single person on a single day the amount of two months, it is not valid except for that day. This is our school. As for al-Shafi'i, tamlik is necessary, as in clothing. The basis of our statement is what is mentioned in usul al-fiqh regarding the indication of the text: 'feeding' means making another eat, and that is by ibaha... etc. The ibaha of food does not renew in a single day. And if he feeds sixty poor people, each a sa' of wheat, for two zihars, it is not valid except for one zihar; but for a broken fast and a zihar, it is valid. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. As for Muhammad, he permits it for two zihars on the basis that intention operates when the types differ, as in breaking fast and zihar, but not when they are the same. So when intention is nullified, and the sa' suffices for one expiation because half a sa' is the minimum amount, then the performed act, which is the sa', suffices for one expiation; he intended it for two zihars, so it is not valid. The specific item becomes an expiation, and that is by owning the item, not by lending, for lending returns to benefit, while ibaha in food fulfills the purpose without lending the garment. There are questions and answers mentioned in al-Talwih. He said: 'And if he feeds...' meaning if he owes two zihar expiations and feeds sixty poor people for both together by giving each a sa' of wheat, intending half a sa' for one zihar and half for the other, it is not valid except for one according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. And if he feeds that for different types, like expiation for breaking Ramadan fast and zihar, it is valid by consensus. Muhammad's proof: In what is performed there is sufficiency for both zihars, and the poor person is the locus for both, so it counts for both as if the cause differed or the poor person differed. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) proof: Intention in a single type is meaningless, and it is considered in different types. When intention is nullified and what is performed suffices for one expiation, it counts for that one.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of feeding sixty poor people with a single sa' each to expiate for two obligations of the same type (e.g., two zihars) versus different types (e.g., zihar and breaking Ramadan fast). The matn states the ruling: feeding sixty poor for two zihars only satisfies one, but for a zihar and a broken fast it satisfies both. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad differs, holding that if the two obligations are of the same type (both zihars), the intention to separate them is valid because the one sa' given to each poor person can cover both expiations since the minimum for each expiation is half a sa'. The commentary explains that according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), intention only distinguishes when the types differ; when they are the same, intention is superfluous because the performance (one sa' per poor person) is sufficient only for one expiation. Therefore, it defaults to one. Muhammad's reasoning is that the performed act (the sa') can fulfill both expiations, and since the poor person is the recipient for both, the intention of the payer splits the expiation. The passage also touches on the method of feeding: the Hanafi position allows feeding via ibaha (making food available) unlike al-Shafi'i who requires tamlik (ownership transfer). This is because the Quranic term 'it'am indicates making someone eat, not giving ownership, and this suffices for the purpose of food.

Key Terms
إباحة (ibāḥa): Making food available for consumption without transferring ownership.
تمليك (tamlīk): Giving ownership of the food to the poor person.
ظهار (ẓihār): A form of divorce where a husband compares his wife to his mother, requiring expiation before resuming marital relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both expiations are discharged.
B) Only one expiation is discharged.
C) Neither expiation is discharged because intention was split.
D) It is invalid because feeding must be done separately.

Key Takeaway
Feeding sixty poor for two identical expiations only counts for one; but for different types, it counts for both.

Feeding 60 Poor for Two Zihar Expiation: Intention and Quantity
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on feeding for two zihar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on feeding for two zihar expiations and apply the rule about intention to determine how many expiations are fulfilled.

Core Idea
Intention differentiates between expiations of different types, but is ineffective when types are the same.

This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about combining expiations. When a person owes two zihar expiations and feeds sixty poor each one sa' of wheat with the intention of fulfilling both, does it suffice for both or only one? The difference hinges on whether intention can differentiate between same-type expiations. We will examine the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and the dissenting view of Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the case
Identify the scenario: a person has two zihar expiations and feeds 60 poor each one sa' of wheat, intending to cover both expiations simultaneously.
2
Identify the positions
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that only one expiation is fulfilled, while Imam Muhammad rules that both are fulfilled.
Both are Hanafi imams; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the proof for the majority
The majority argue that intention is only effective when the expiations are of different types (e.g., zihar and breaking Ramadan fast). When they are the same type, intention is void. Since the given quantity (one sa' per poor) is sufficient for only one expiation (the minimum being half a sa' per poor per expiation, but the total given per poor is one sa' which is enough for one, not two), the act fulfills only one.
The key principle: niyyah is for discrimination, not for increasing quantity.
4
Analyze the proof for Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad argues that since the total amount given (60 sa') is enough for two expiations (each requiring 30 sa'), the act suffices for both. He considers the quantity sufficient and does not require intention to differentiate within the same type.
For Imam Muhammad, the absence of intention does not void when the quantity is sufficient.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: only one expiation is fulfilled. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The commentary supports the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أطعم ستين مسكيناً كلاً صاعاً من بر عن ظهارين لم يصح إلا عن ظهار واحد، وعن إفطار وظهار صح، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وأما عند محمد فيجوز عن الظهارين هما يقولان النيَّةُ تعمل عند اختلافِ الجنسين كالإفطار والظهار، لا عند اتحادِهما، فإذا لَغَت النية والصاعُ يصلح كفارة واحدة؛ لأنَّ نصف الصَّاع من أدنى المقادير، فالمؤدى وهو الصاع يصلح كفارة واحدة جَعَلَها للظهارين فلا يصح يصير العين كفارة، وذا بتمليك العين لا بالإعارة، إذ هي ترد على المنفعة على أنَّ الإباحة في الطعام تتم المقصود دون إعارة الثوب. انتهى. وفي المقام أسئلة وأجوبة مذكورة في «التلويح». قوله : وإن أطعم ... الخ؛ يعني لو كانت عليه كفارة ظهارين فأطعم ستين مسكيناً عنهما معاً بأن أعطى كلاً منهم صاعاً من حنطة ، ونوى نصف صاع من ظهار ونصفه من آخر لم يجزه إلا عن واحدٍ منهما عندهما خلافاً لمحمد له، وإن أطعم ذلك عن مختلفي الجنس ككفّارة إفطار رمضان، وكفارة ظهار أجزأ عنهما اتفاقاً. له : أنّ في المؤدي وفاء بالظهارين، والفقير المصروف إليه محلّ لهما، فيقع عنهما كما عنه اختلاف السبب واختلاف الفقير. ولهما : إنّ النية في الجنس الواحد لغو، وتعتبر في الجنسين، وإذا لغت النية والمؤدّي يصلح كونه لكفارة واحدة، فيقع عنها. قوله : فإذا لغت النية...الخ؛ قال في «الفتح» : لأن النية إنما تعتبر التمييز
If he feeds sixty poor each a sa' of wheat for two zihar (expiation), it is not valid except for one zihar, and for (expiation of) breaking fast and zihar it is valid. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. As for Muhammad, he permits it for the two zihar. They both say: intention is effective when the types differ, like breaking fast and zihar, not when they are the same. So when the intention is void, and the sa' suffices for one expiation, because half a sa' is the minimum amount, so what is given, which is a sa', suffices for one expiation, if he makes it for two zihar, it is not valid. The thing becomes expiation by transferring ownership, not by lending, because it pertains to benefit, and permission in food accomplishes the purpose without lending a garment. End. And in this context there are questions and answers mentioned in al-Talwih. He said: (His saying: ...) meaning: if he owed expiation for two zihar and fed sixty poor for both together by giving each a sa' of wheat, intending half a sa' for one zihar and half for the other, it is not permissible except for one of them according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. If he fed for different types, like expiation for breaking Ramadan fast and expiation for zihar, it suffices for both by agreement. His proof: that in what is given there is fulfillment of both zihar expiations, and the poor person to whom it is given is a place for both, so it occurs for both just as the difference of cause and difference of poor person. Their (the two's) proof: that intention concerning the same type is void, and is considered concerning two types; when intention is void and what is given suffices for one expiation, it occurs for that one. He said: (His saying: when intention is void...) He said in al-Fath: because intention is only considered for discrimination.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding feeding sixty poor people for two zihar expiations. The ruling stated by the author is that if a person feeds sixty poor each with one sa' of wheat intending it for two zihar expiations, it only fulfills one expiation, not both. However, if the expiations are of different types, such as one for zihar and one for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast, it suffices for both. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that intention is only effective when the expiations are of different types; when they are the same type, the intention is void. Since the amount given (one sa' per poor) is sufficient for only one expiation (the minimum per expiation is half a sa' per poor, but the total given suffices for one), it is counted as one. Imam Muhammad argues that it suffices for both because the payment of two sa' (since each poor gets one sa', total 60 sa' for 60 poor) is enough to cover two expiations, and the intention is not needed when the quantity is sufficient. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The commentary explains that if the expiations are of the same type, the intention does not differentiate, so only one is fulfilled. If the types differ, intention is effective.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention that differentiates between expiations; effective when expiations are of different types but not when they are the same type.
ظهار (zihar): A form of divorce where a husband says to his wife 'you are like my mother's back', requiring expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, feeding 60 poor each one sa' of wheat for two zihar expiations fulfills how many expiations?
A) Two expiations
B) One expiation
C) None, because the intention was shared
D) It depends on the value of the food

Key Takeaway
Intention is crucial for differentiating expiations of different types; for same-type expiations, intention is ineffective and only one expiation is fulfilled if the amount suffices for only one.

Ruling on Two Zihar Expiations: Unity of Type and Specification
Ruling on multiple expiation acts for two zihar expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fulfilling multiple zihar expiations and explain why specific intention is not required when the type is unitary.

Core Idea
When expiations are of the same type, no specification needed — unity of type removes the requirement of ta'ayyun.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario in zihar: a man owes two kaffarah for two zihar pronouncements. The text explains how he can discharge them by fasting, feeding, or freeing slaves, and whether he must intend each act for a specific expiation. The key principle is 'unity of type' (ittihad al-jins), which determines the need for specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case: a man owes two zihar expiations (kaffaratayn al-zihar). Note the cause (sabab) is the same for both.
Zihar is a form of divorce-like declaration that requires expiation.
2
Determine the expiation acts
The text lists three possible acts: fasting (four consecutive months), feeding (120 poor), or freeing slaves (two slaves). The quantity matches the total for two expiations.
For one zihar expiation, the options are: fast 2 months, feed 60 poor, or free one slave.
3
Apply the rule of unitary type
Since both expiations are for zihar, the type (jins) is the same. Per Hanafi fiqh, when the type is unitary, no specific intention (ta'ayyun) is needed for each act. The combined performance suffices.
Specification becomes necessary only when types differ (e.g., oath and zihar).
4
Contrast with single act or different types
If only one slave is freed or two months are fasted for both expiations, the person may specify which expiation he intends, as the act is only sufficient for one. If expiations are of different types, each act must be intended for a specific expiation.
The text gives the example of oath, killing, and zihar expiations together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كصوم أربعة أشهر ، أو إطعام مئة وعشرين مسكيناً ، أو إعتاق عبدين عن ظهارين، وإن لم يعين واحداً لواحد) ؛ لأنَّ الجنس في الظهارين متحد فلا يجب التعين. (وفي إعتاق عبد عنهما ، أو صوم شهرين ، له أن يعين لأي شاء). [١]قوله : كصوم ؛ تشبية بما تقدّم في الصحة ، يعني إذا كانت عليه كفارتا ظهار، فصام أربعة أشهر، كل شهرين متتابعين، أو أطعم مئة وعشرين مسكيناً إباحة أو تمليكاً أو أعتق عبدين، كل ذلك بنية كفارتي الظهار، أجزأه ذلك عنهما ؛ لأنَّ الجنس متحد، فلا يحتاج إلى نية معينة. بخلاف اختلاف الجنس، كما لو كانت عليه كفّارة يمين، وكفارة قتل، وكفارة ظهار، فأعتق عبيداً عن الكفارات لم يجز، ولو أعتق كلّ رقبة ناوياً عن أحدها بعينها أو لا بعينها جاز ، ولم تضرّ جهالة المكفّر . عنه. كذا في «البحر» عن «المحيط». [٢]قوله : متحد ؛ اتحاد الجنس في هذا الباب يعرف باتحاد السبب الموجب للكفّارة، واختلافه باختلاف. [٣) قوله : له ؛ أي للمظاهر المكفّر أن يجعل عتقه وصومه لأي من الظهارين شاء
Like fasting four months, or feeding one hundred and twenty poor, or freeing two slaves for two zihar expiations, even if he does not specify one for one; because the type in the two zihar is unitary, so specification is not required. (And in freeing a slave for both, or fasting two months, he may specify for whichever he wishes). [1] His saying: like fasting; analogy to what preceded in validity, meaning if he owes expiation for two zihar, and he fasts four months, each two consecutive, or feeds one hundred and twenty poor by permission or ownership, or frees two slaves, all with intention of the two zihar expiations, it suffices for both; because the type is unitary, so a specific intention is not needed. Contrary to difference of type, as if he owes expiation for an oath, expiation for killing, and expiation for zihar, and he frees slaves for the expiations, it is not permissible; but if he frees each slave intending a specific one or not specific, it is permissible, and ignorance of which expiation is not harmful. Thus in al-Bahr from al-Muhit. [2] His saying: unitary; unity of type in this chapter is known by unity of the cause that obligates the expiation, and its difference by difference. [3] His saying: for him; meaning for the one who declared zihar (the expiating person) to make his freeing or fasting for whichever of the two zihar he wishes.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for multiple expiation acts covering two zihar expiations. The author states that if a person fasts four consecutive months (two for each zihar), feeds one hundred and twenty poor (sixty for each), or frees two slaves (one for each zihar), it suffices for both without needing to specify which act covers which expiation. This is because the type (jins) of the expiations is the same (both are zihar), so specific intention is not required. However, if he only frees one slave or fasts two months intending it for both, he may specify which zihar he is covering, because the act is only sufficient for one expiation, so he must choose. The commentary also notes that if the expiations are of different types (e.g., oath, killing, and zihar), then freeing multiple slaves without specifying which slave is for which does not count; each slave must be intended for a specific expiation or at least left unspecified generally. The unit of type is determined by the cause that obligates the expiation: if the cause (like zihar) is the same, the type is the same; if causes differ, types differ.

Key Terms
الجنس (al-jins): The type or category of expiation; here, zihar expiations are of the same type, so no specification is needed.
تعين (ta'ayyun): Specification of intention for a particular expiation; not required when the type is unitary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what determines whether specific intention is required for multiple expiation acts?
A) The number of expiations
B) The type of expiation (jins)
C) The quantity of the act
D) The intention of the person

Key Takeaway
When multiple zihar expiations are owed, performing the combined quantity of the expiation acts suffices without specifying each part, as long as the type is unitary.

When Intention Suffices: Expiating Multiple Zihars and the Hanafi Position on Unity of Type
Ruling on expiating two zihars with one act and dispute with Zufar/Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between unified and different types of expiation (kaffarah) and apply the Hanafi rule that specific intention (niyyat ta'yin) is required only when the types differ, and evaluate the conflicting views of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
When the cause of expiation is the same, intention does not need to specify; when causes differ, specification is required.

This passage from al-Hidayah's commentary explains a key principle regarding expiation of multiple zihars or combined expiations. The central question is whether a single expiatory act (e.g., fasting two consecutive months) can simultaneously expiate two zihars without the need to specify which month is for which zihar. The Hanafi ruling hinges on the concept of whether the expiations belong to the same type (jins) or different types, which in turn depends on the underlying cause (sabab). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying expiation rules in complex cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on same-type expiations
From the base text: if two zihar expiations are due, fasting four consecutive months (two months for each), feeding 120 poor, or freeing two slaves suffices for both without specifying which act is for which zihar. This is because the type is unified.
Type unity is determined by unity of the cause obligating the expiation.
2
Identify the ruling on different-type expiations
If the expiations are for different causes (e.g., oath, killing, zihar), freeing slaves for all does not suffice unless the intention specifies each slave for a particular expiation. If specified, it suffices even if the expiation is unknown.
Ignorance of which expiation is expiated does not harm after specification.
3
Understand the Hanafi definition of unity of type (jins)
The commentary states: 'Unity of type in this chapter is known by the unity of the cause obligating the expiation, and difference by difference.' Thus, two zihars have the same cause, so they are the same type.
Cause (sabab) = the act that triggers the expiation (e.g., making zihar, killing, breaking an oath).
4
Analyze the opposing views: Zufar and al-Shafi'i
Zufar argues that freeing one slave for two expiations is like freeing half a slave for each, so it suffices for neither. Al-Shafi'i argues that all expiations are one type due to unity of purpose, so general intention suffices.
Zufar's view is within the Hanafi school (a disciple of Abu Hanifa). Al-Shafi'i's view represents the Shafi'i school.
5
Apply the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: Unity of purpose does not necessitate unity of type; the cause is the basis for distinction. Specific intention is beneficial in different types and cannot be changed, whereas in same type it is ineffective and thus disregarded.
This reasoning is from al-Hidayah and is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كصوم أربعة أشهر ، أو إطعام مئة وعشرين مسكيناً ، أو إعتاق عبدين عن ظهارين، وإن لم يعين واحداً لواحد، وفي إعتاق عبد عنهما ، أو صوم شهرين له أن يعين لأي شاء.
[١]قوله : كصوم ؛ تشبية بما تقدّم في الصحة ، يعني إذا كانت عليه كفارتا ظهار، فصام أربعة أشهر، كل شهرين متتابعين، أو أطعم مئة وعشرين مسكيناً إباحة أو تمليكاً أو أعتق عبدين، كل ذلك بنية كفارتي الظهار، أجزأه ذلك عنهما ؛ لأنَّ الجنس متحد، فلا يحتاج إلى نية معينة. بخلاف اختلاف الجنس، كما لو كانت عليه كفّارة يمين، وكفارة قتل، وكفارة ظهار، فأعتق عبيداً عن الكفارات لم يجز، ولو أعتق كلّ رقبة ناوياً عن أحدها بعينها أو لا بعينها جاز ، ولم تضرّ جهالة المكفّر عنه. كذا في «البحر» عن «المحيط».
[٢]قوله : متحد ؛ اتحاد الجنس في هذا الباب يعرف باتحاد السبب الموجب للكفّارة، واختلافه باختلاف. [٣) قوله : له ؛ أي للمظاهر المكفّر أن يجعل عتقه وصومه لأي من الظهارين شاء،
وإن أعتق عن قتل وظهار لم يجز عن واحد، وعند زُفَر له لا يجزيه عن أحدهما في الفصلين ، وعند الشَّافِعِي له يجعل عن أحدهما في الفصلين).
[١]قوله : في الفصلين ؛ أي في مختلف الجنس ومتحده.
وجه قول زفر : إنه لما أعتق عبداً عنهما ، فصار كأنه أعتق عن كل ظهار أو ظهار وقتل نصف العبد ولا يمكن أن يجعله عن أحدهما بعدما أعتق عنهما ؛ لخروج الأمر من اختياره. ووجه قول الشافعي : إنّ الكفارات كلّها باعتبار اتحاد المقصودِ جنس واحد ، وإن كان السبب مختلفاً، والنية في الجنس الواحدة ملغاة، فبقيت نية أصل الكفّارة، ولو نوى أصل الكفّارة كان له أن يجعلَ عن أيهما شاء، فكذا هذا.
ونحن نقول : إنّ اتحاد المقصود لا يلزم كون الكفارات كلها جنساً واحداً، بل بسبب اختلاف السبب يختلف الجنس، ونيّة التعيين في الجنس المتحد غير مفيدة فتلغو، فبقى مطلق النيّة ، فله أن يصرفه إلى ما شاء، وفي الجنس المختلف مفيدة ، فلا يمكن له تغيرها. كذا في «الهداية» وحواشيها.
[Base text:] Like fasting four months, or feeding one hundred and twenty poor persons, or freeing two slaves for two zihars, and if he did not specify one for one. And in freeing one slave for both, or fasting two months, he may specify for whichever he wishes. [Commentary:] (His saying: 'like fasting...') is a comparison to what preceded in validity, meaning: if two zihar expiations are due on him, and he fasts four months (two consecutive months each), or feeds one hundred twenty poor persons (by permission or ownership), or frees two slaves, all with the intention of the two zihar expiations, it suffices for both, because the type is unified, so specific intention is not needed. Unlike differing types, as if he had an oath expiation, a killing expiation, and a zihar expiation, and he freed slaves for the expiations, it does not suffice. If he freed each slave intending one specifically or not specifically, it suffices, and ignorance of which expiation is expiated does not harm. (From al-Bahr, quoting al-Muhit.) (His saying: 'unified'): Unity of type in this chapter is known by the unity of the cause obligating expiation, and difference by difference. (His saying: 'for him'): i.e., for the mazhir (one who made zihar) who is expiating, that he may make his freeing and fasting for whichever of the two zihars he wishes. And if he freed for killing and zihar, it does not suffice for either. According to Zufar, it does not suffice for one of them in both cases (united and different types). According to al-Shafi'i, he may make it for one of them in both cases. (Commentary on 'in both cases': i.e., in different and same type.) The reasoning of Zufar: Because when he freed a slave for both, it becomes as if he freed half a slave for each zihar or for each killing, and he cannot make it for one after having freed for both, because the matter has left his choice. The reasoning of al-Shafi'i: Because all expiations, considering the unity of purpose, are one type, even if the cause differs, and intention in a single type is disregarded, so the intention of the original expiation remains; if he intended the original expiation, he could make it for whichever he wishes, and so too here. And we (Hanafis) say: The unity of purpose does not necessitate that all expiations are one type; rather, due to differing causes, the type differs. Specific intention in a unified type is not beneficial and is disregarded, so absolute intention remains, and he may direct it as he wishes. In differing types, it is beneficial, so he cannot change it. (From al-Hidayah and its glosses.)
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on expiating multiple zihars or a combination of zihar with other types of expiations. The base text states that if a person has two zihar expiations, he can fulfill both by fasting four months (two consecutive months for each), feeding one hundred twenty poor persons, or freeing two slaves, without needing to specify which expiation is for which zihar. However, if he frees one slave or fasts one month for both, he must specify which zihar he intends. The commentary explains the principle: when the type (jins) of expiation is the same (i.e., same cause, e.g., two zihars), specific intention is not required because the genus is unified. But when the causes differ (e.g., zihar and killing), the types differ, and specific intention becomes necessary. A dispute is then presented: Imam Zufar holds that if one act is intended for two different expiations, it does not suffice for either, because it is like freeing half a slave for each. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that all expiations are one type due to unity of purpose, so intention of the original expiation suffices. The Hanafi position (stated in 'we say') rejects this, asserting that differing causes create different types, and specific intention is required for different types, but not for the same type. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi view is that for same-type expiations, general intention suffices; for different types, specific intention is necessary.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A man saying to his wife 'you are like my mother's back', which makes her unlawful until expiation.
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory act (fasting, feeding, or freeing) required to remove the sin and permit marital relations.
نية تعيين (niyyat ta'yin): Specific intention to which expiation the act is for; required when types differ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has two zihar expiations. He fasts two consecutive months with the general intention of 'expiating both zihars'. According to Hanafi fiqh, is his fast valid?
A) Yes, because the type is unified and specific intention is not required.
B) No, because each zihar must be expiated separately.
C) It is invalid unless he also feeds the poor.
D) It depends on whether he also freed a slave.

Key Takeaway
When expiating multiple obligations, Hanafi law distinguishes between same-type expiations (same cause → no specific intention needed) and different-type expiations (different causes → specific intention required).

Slave's Zihar: Expiation Only by Fasting
Ruling that a slave's kaffarah for zihar is fasting only

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's kaffarah for zihar and explain why fasting is the only valid option.

Core Idea
A slave who makes zihar must fast because he owns nothing.

Zihar is a prohibited form of divorce, and it requires expiation. For a free person, there are three options: freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding the poor. But what if the person who commits zihar is a slave himself? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling: a slave cannot choose freeing or feeding because he possesses no property—everything in his hand belongs to his master. Therefore, the only way for him to expiate is by fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is zihar performed by a slave. The ruling is that expiation (kaffarah) is wajib upon him, but limited to fasting only.
This applies to all categories of slaves: qinn (pure slave), mukatib, mudabbar, etc.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the reason given: the slave owns nothing. The text states 'because he owns nothing, and indeed everything in his hand is the property of the master.' This is the operative cause (illah).
The dalil is not a revealed text but a clear deduction from the slave's legal incapacity to own property.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The link: the expiation options of freeing a slave or feeding require possession or disposal of property. Since the slave lacks that, those options are invalid. Fasting requires no property, so it remains valid.
The master cannot prevent the slave from fasting because it is an act of worship.
4
Note ikhtilaf
No intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute is mentioned in this passage. The Hanafi school is unanimous on this ruling.
Some other schools may hold a different view, but this passage does not discuss it.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. It is relied upon without exception in the Hanafi school.
The authority weight is high; there is no conflicting view within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وكفر ... الخ؛ يعني إذا ظاهر عبد من امرأته سواء كان قناً خالصاً أو مكاتباً أو مدبراً أو غير ذلك، فكفارته لا تكون إلا بالصوم لا بالإعتاق ولا بالإطعام؛ لأنه لا يملك شيئاً، فإنّ كلَّ ما في يده ملك المولى، ولا يمنعه المولى من هذا الصوم؛ لأنه
His saying: 'and the expiation of a slave who made zihar...' etc.; meaning: if a slave makes zihar to his wife, whether he is a pure slave, a mukatib, a mudabbar, or otherwise, his expiation is only by fasting, not by freeing nor by feeding, because he owns nothing, and indeed everything in his hand is the property of the master, and the master does not prevent him from this fasting because...
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on a slave who declares zihar. The key point is that a slave has no ownership of property; everything in his possession belongs to his master. Therefore, the options of freeing a slave or feeding the poor are unavailable to him, as they require ownership or disposal of property. The only valid form of expiation for a slave is fasting. The commentary also notes that the master cannot prevent the slave from fasting, as it is an act of worship required for the expiation. The text is cut off before stating the duration of the fast (likely two consecutive months), but the ruling is clear: the slave's kaffarah is exclusively by fasting.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): A male slave who is owned by another; includes various categories like qinn, mukatib, mudabbar.
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has a contract with his master to purchase his freedom in installments.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is promised freedom upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the only valid form of kaffarah for a slave who makes zihar?
A) Freeing a slave
B) Feeding sixty poor persons
C) Fasting two consecutive months
D) Any of the above, with the master's permission

Key Takeaway
A slave's zihar expiation is exclusively by fasting because he lacks ownership of property.

Dispute on Intention in Combined Kaffara for Murder and Zihar
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on freedom of intention in combined kaffara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combined kaffara and compare it with the Shafi'i view, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
One emancipation cannot satisfy two different types of kaffara; intention binds expiation to its cause.

This passage tackles a practical scenario where a person tries to fulfill two expiations (for murder and zihar) with a single act of emancipation. The Hanafi school insists that the difference in causes makes the kaffaras different types, requiring separate acts. A competing view from Imam al-Shafi'i argues for unity of purpose. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how intention (niyya) functions in different obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two obligations
The act is emancipating a slave with the intention of fulfilling both kaffara for murder (qatl) and zihar. Note that both kaffaras, in their standard form, require emancipating a believing slave.
The passage assumes the person explicitly intends both.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to Abu Hanifa and the Hanafi school, the emancipation does not fulfill either obligation. The act is batil (invalid) for both kaffaras.
3
Understand Zufar's rationale
Zufar (within the Hanafi school) agrees: emancipating one slave for both obligations is like freeing half a slave for each, and after emancipation, the person loses the ability to choose which obligation to fulfill.
Zufar's view is consistent with the Hanafi position.
4
Analyze al-Shafi'i's argument
Imam al-Shafi'i contends that all kaffaras are one type because they share the same purpose (expiation). Therefore, intention is disregarded, and the general intent to perform kaffara suffices. After the act, the person may assign it to either obligation at his choice.
5
Grasp the Hanafi counter
The Hanafi response: Unity of purpose does not erase type differences. Different causes (murder vs. zihar) create different types of kaffara. In a single type, intention is ineffective, but in different types, specifying intention is decisive and cannot be changed after the act.
The author cites al-Hidayah as authority for this response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أعتق عن قتل وظهار لم يجز عن واحد، وعند زُفَر له لا يجزتُهُ عن أحدهما في الفصلين، وعند الشَّافِعِي له يُجْعَلُ عن أحدهما في الفصلين). قوله : في الفصلين؛ أي في مختلف الجنس ومتحده. وجه قول زفر: إنه لما أعتق عبداً عنهما، فصار كأنه أعتق عن كل ظهار أو ظهار وقتل نصف العبد ولا يمكن أن يجعله عن أحدهما بعدما أعتق عنهما؛ لخروج الأمر من اختياره. ووجه قول الشافعي: إنّ الكفارات كلّها باعتبار اتحاد المقصودِ جنس واحد، وإن كان السبب مختلفاً، والنية في الجنس الواحدة ملغاة، فبقيت نية أصل الكفّارة، ولو نوى أصل الكفّارة كان له أن يجعلَ عن أيهما شاء، فكذا هذا. ونحن نقول: إنّ اتحاد المقصود لا يلزم كون الكفارات كلها جنساً واحداً، بل بسبب اختلاف السبب يختلف الجنس، ونيّة التعيين في الجنس المتحد غير مفيدة فتلغو، فبقى مطلق النيّة، فله أن يصرفه إلى ما شاء، وفي الجنس المختلف مفيدة، فلا يمكن له تغيرها. كذا في «الهداية» وحواشيها.
And if he emancipates for murder and zihar, it is not valid for either. According to Zufar, it is not valid for either in both cases. According to al-Shafi'i, it is made valid for either in both cases. He said: 'In both cases' means in different and same category. The basis of Zufar's statement: When he emancipated a slave for both, it becomes as if he emancipated for each zihar or zihar and murder half a slave, and it is not possible to assign it to one after having emancipated for both, because the matter is out of his choice. The basis of al-Shafi'i's statement: All expiations, by virtue of unity of purpose, are one type, even if the cause differs, and intention in a single type is disregarded, so the intention for expiation in general remains; and if he intended expiation in general, he could assign it to whichever he wishes, so similarly here. And we say: Unity of purpose does not necessitate that all expiations are one type; rather, due to difference of cause, the type differs, and specifying intention in a unified type is not beneficial and is disregarded, so general intention remains, and he may direct it as he wishes; in a different type, it is beneficial, so he cannot change it. Thus in al-Hidayah and its glosses.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding a person who emancipates a slave intending to fulfill kaffara for both murder (qatl) and zihar. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that the emancipation does not satisfy either obligation because the two kaffaras are of different types (murder requires emancipation of a believing slave, zihar requires general emancipation; in some views, they are the same type). The text clarifies that according to Zufar (a Hanafi jurist), the emancipation is also invalid for either in both cases (whether the causes are of the same type or different). According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the emancipation is valid for one of them at the choice of the person. The argument for Zufar's view is that emancipating one slave for two obligations effectively emancipates half a slave for each, and the choice is removed after emancipation. Al-Shafi'i argues that all kaffaras are one type due to the unity of purpose (expiation), so intention is disregarded, and the general intention suffices, allowing him to assign it to either. The Hanafi response is that unity of purpose does not make all kaffaras one type; different causes create different types, so specifying intention is beneficial and cannot be changed. In the same type, intention is disregarded, but here the types differ, so the initial intention to combine is ineffective. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the emancipation does not count for either kaffara, as stated in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A form of divorce-like declaration where a husband says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back,' requiring kaffara before resuming relations.
كفارة (kaffara): Expiation for sins or broken oaths; here specifically for murder and zihar, involving emancipation, fasting, or feeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, if a person emancipates a slave intending it to cover kaffara for both murder and zihar, what is the ruling?
A) It fulfills one of the two kaffaras.
B) It fulfills both kaffaras.
C) It fulfills neither kaffara.
D) It invalidates the emancipation.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, kaffara obligations are defined by their causes; a single act cannot simultaneously fulfill two different types, and a specifying intention once acted upon cannot be reassigned.

Slave's Kaffara for Zihar: Only Fasting Permissible
Ruling statement with explanatory objection-response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a slave's kaffara for zihar is limited to fasting two consecutive months, and explain why worship is not halved for slaves.

Core Idea
A slave's zihar kaffara must be a complete fast—worship is not halved, only punishments and benefits are.

When a slave performs zihar, his expiation is uniquely restricted. Unlike a free person who may choose between emancipation, fasting, or feeding, the slave can only fast. Moreover, his master cannot pay the kaffara on his behalf. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its underlying principle: acts of worship are personal and indivisible, while punishments and worldly benefits are halved for slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zihar by a slave. The ruling is that the slave must perform kaffara by fasting two consecutive months (sawm shahrayn mutatabi'ayn). This is wajib.
The passage explicitly says 'by fasting only' (بالصوم فقط).
2
Explain why alternatives (emancipation, feeding) are unavailable
A slave owns no wealth and no slave of his own, so emancipation and feeding are impossible. Only fasting is possible and thus obligatory.
This follows the principle that obligation is according to ability.
3
Address the objection: why is fasting not halved?
The text anticipates a question: since slaves are halved in many rulings (e.g., hudud, marriage), why is the fasting not half? The answer: worship (ibadah) is not halved; it is a personal act that cannot be divided. Only punishments (uqubat) and benefits (ni'am) are halved.
This is a key Hanafi distinction between categories of rulings.
4
Rule on master's payment
The master cannot pay the kaffara with wealth on the slave's behalf, whether commanded or not. Reason: the slave does not own wealth, and one person's worship cannot be performed by another.
This reinforces the personal nature of worship-based obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكفر عبد ظاهر فله وطء التي كفّر عن ظهارها دون الأخرى. بالصوم فقط لا سيده بالمال عنه. قوله: بالصوم؛ أي صوم شهرين متتابعين. إن قلت: كيف لزمه الصوم المذكور ولم يجب عليه نصفه، مع أنَّ العبد على التنصيف في أكثر الأحكام؟ قلت: صوم الكفارة فيه معنى العبادة والعبادة لا تتنصف على العبيد، وإنما تتنصف العقوبة كالحد، والنعمة كالنكاح وما يتعلق بهما. قوله: لا سيده؛ أي لا يجزئ أن يكفّر بالمال عنه سيده، سواء كان بأمره أو بغير أمره؛ لعدم تملكه شيئاً من المال، وعبادة رجلٍ لا تقع عن آخر.
And a slave makes kaffara for zihar, so he may have intercourse with the woman for whose zihar he made kaffara, not the other. Only by fasting, not his master on his behalf with wealth. He said: 'by fasting' means fasting two consecutive months. If you say: How is the mentioned fasting incumbent upon him and not half of it, given that a slave is halved in most rulings? I say: Fasting of kaffara contains the meaning of worship, and worship is not halved for slaves; rather, punishment is halved like hudud, and benefit like marriage and what relates to them. He said: 'not his master' means it is not valid for his master to make kaffara with wealth on his behalf, whether by his command or not, because he does not own any wealth, and one person's worship does not occur on behalf of another.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on a slave's kaffara for zihar. When a slave performs zihar, his expiation can only be fasting (two consecutive months), not emancipation (since he owns no slave) nor feeding (since he does not own wealth). Moreover, his master cannot pay kaffara on his behalf with money, because the slave does not own wealth, and acts of worship are personal. Once the slave completes the fast, he may resume relations with the wife he declared zihar on. The commentary addresses a potential objection: since slaves generally receive half punishment and half rights, why is the full fast required? The answer is that acts of worship are not halved; only punishments (hudud) and benefits (like marriage) are halved. This is based on the principle that worship is personal and cannot be split.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffara): Expiation for zihar, which for a slave is restricted to fasting two consecutive months.
صوم شهرين متتابعين (sawm shahrayn mutatabi'ayn): Fasting two consecutive months without interruption; if broken, must restart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A slave's kaffara for zihar is exclusively fasting two consecutive months; worship is personal and not halved, and the master cannot substitute it with wealth.

Slave's Zihar Expiation: Fasting Only, Master Cannot Pay
Ruling that slave must fast for zihar, master cannot pay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a slave's zihar expiation, explain why the master cannot pay, and resolve the apparent conflict with the principle of halving for slaves.

Core Idea
A slave's zihar expiation is worship – not halved and not payable by the master.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter of Zihar: a slave who commits zihar must expiate by fasting two consecutive months, and his master cannot pay a monetary expiation on his behalf. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling, including why the fast is not halved despite the general principle that slaves are treated as half in many rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and the act
Identify that the act is zihar committed by a slave, and the ruling is that expiation is wajib by fasting only, not by freeing a slave or feeding (since slave cannot own wealth). The master cannot pay money for him.
2
Understand the primary proof: expiation is worship
The text states that expiation is an act of worship, so the act of another cannot be considered the slave's act. Therefore, the master's payment does not discharge the slave's obligation.
3
Resolve the objection about halving
The objection: why isn't the fast halved to one month, since slaves are subject to halving in many rulings? The answer: worship is not halved; only penalties (like hadd) and benefits (like marriage) are halved. Expiation is worship, not a penalty.
4
Distinguish from other expiations
In other expiations (e.g., for accidental killing), the master may prevent the slave from fasting if it harms his service. Here, the wife has a right attached, so the master cannot prevent the fast.
5
Apply the principle of personal obligation
The rule that worship is personal and cannot be performed by another is key. It applies to all acts of worship, not just expiation.

فعله.

The chapter of Zihar from the Book of Talaq. By fasting only, not his master (paying) with wealth on his behalf. By fasting only, not his master with wealth on his behalf; because the expiation is an act of worship, so the act of another is not his act. The right of the woman is attached to it, unlike the rest of expiations, for he may prevent him from fasting if it is detrimental to his service, because no right of a slave is attached to it. Likewise in 'al-Bahr'. (1) His saying: 'by fasting' means fasting two consecutive months. If you say: How is the mentioned fasting incumbent upon him and half is not obligatory on him, whereas the slave is subject to halving in most rulings? I say: Fasting of expiation has the meaning of worship, and worship is not halved for slaves; rather, punishment is halved like hadd, and benefit like marriage and what pertains to them. (2) His saying: 'not his master' means that it is not permissible for his master to expiate with wealth on his behalf, whether by his command or otherwise, because the slave does not own any wealth, and the worship of one man does not occur for another. (1) (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, 4:115).
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter of Zihar, specifically concerning a slave's expiation. The text states that a slave who has engaged in zihar must fast two consecutive months for expiation, and his master cannot pay a monetary expiation on his behalf. The reason given is that expiation is an act of worship (عبادة), and the act of one person cannot stand in for another's act of worship. However, unlike other expiations, here the master cannot even prevent the slave from fasting because the wife has a right attached to this expiation. The commentary then addresses an objection: why must the slave fast the full two months? Since slaves are generally treated as half in many rulings (e.g., in hudud punishments, half the penalty applies). The answer: expiation (kaffara) is a form of worship, and worship is not halved for slaves; only penalties (like hadd) and benefits (like marriage) are halved. Finally, the text clarifies that the master cannot pay with wealth at all, because the slave owns nothing, and one person's worship cannot be performed by another. This ruling is from the Hanafi school as recorded in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Key Terms
الظهار (al-zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother', requiring expiation before intercourse.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation required for zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two months consecutively, or feeding sixty poor.
التنصيف (al-tansif): The principle that slaves are treated as half in certain rulings like penalties and benefits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't a master pay the expiation for his slave in zihar?
A) Because the slave owns nothing and worship of one cannot substitute for another.
B) Because the master is not allowed to engage in financial transactions for the slave.
C) Because the expiation is a punishment and punishments are not halved for slaves.
D) Because the master has no right to interfere in the slave's marital affairs.

Key Takeaway
A slave's zihar expiation is a personal act of worship – it must be performed by the slave through fasting, and the master cannot pay on his behalf.

Definition and Conditions of Li'an
Definition and conditions of li'an with Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of li'an, identify its Quranic basis, and list the conditions for its validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Li'an replaces hadd when a husband accuses his wife without witnesses.

This lesson introduces li'an (mutual cursing), a unique procedure in Islamic law that resolves accusations of adultery between spouses without external witnesses. The passage defines the term, cites its Quranic foundation, and outlines the conditions under which li'an is valid. Understanding these conditions is crucial because invalid li'an does not prevent hadd punishment.

Guided Path
1
Define li'an linguistically and legally
Explain the etymology from 'la'n' (curse) and the legal definition as sworn testimonies with curses replacing the hadd of slander for the husband and hadd of adultery for the wife.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Recognize that Surah An-Nur 24:6-9 is the primary dalil, establishing the procedure of li'an when a husband accuses his wife without witnesses.
3
Differentiate li'an from qadhf of non-spouse
Note that accusing a non-mahram woman leads to the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes), not li'an.
4
List the essential conditions
Mention that valid marriage (nikah sahih), freedom, puberty, sanity, Islam, speech, and absence of prior hadd for slander are required. Both parties must be qualified to testify.
5
Understand the effect of conditions
Invalid marriage, final divorce (bain), or death of the wife prevents li'an; revocable divorce (raj'i) allows it. Conditions apply to both spouses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter of Li'an. Chapter of Li'an. (Whoever accuses his chaste wife of adultery. [1] [1] His saying: Chapter of Li'an; it - with kasra on the lam. 6 Source of la'an; like qatala, like mula'anah, and its origin from la'n, which is expulsion and distancing from the mercy of Allah. Legally, it is expressions of testimonies emphasized by oaths accompanied by cursing, standing in place of the hadd of slander on his part and the hadd of adultery on her part; meaning if they perform li'an, the hadd of slander is dropped from him and the hadd of adultery from her. Its basis is His statement: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves, then the testimony of one of them is four testimonies by Allah that he is among the truthful, and the fifth that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars. And it shall avert the punishment from her if she testifies four testimonies by Allah that he is among the liars, and the fifth that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful.' (Surah An-Nur, 24:6-9). These verses indicate that li'an is only for accusing the wife. As for a foreign woman, accusing her necessitates the hadd, as stated before these verses in His statement: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, lash them eighty lashes.' And that in the absence of witnesses, if the husband brings four witnesses to her adultery, there is no li'an and no hadd on him, rather she is punished with the hadd of adultery. Likewise, if she confesses to adultery and confirms the husband. In summary: Li'an only occurs when a man accuses his wife of adultery, she denies it, and he does not bring witnesses. And that the pillar of li'an is the four testimonies, hence it is conditional that both be from those who are qualified to give testimony. [2] His saying: 'his wife'; mentioned in 'al-Bahr' and others that its condition is the existence of marriage by a valid contract (nikah sahih). So there is no li'an by accusing a spouse in a fasid marriage or a divorced woman, even with one divorce, unlike a revocably divorced woman (raj'iyyah). Nor by accusing his deceased wife. Also required are freedom, puberty, sanity, Islam, speech, and absence of hadd for slander. These are conditions pertaining to both. (1) An-Nur: 6-9. (2) An-Nur: from the verse. (3) (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, 4:122-123).
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on Li'an (mutual cursing). It first defines the term linguistically and legally: linguistically, li'an is derived from la'n (curse) meaning expulsion from mercy; legally, it consists of sworn testimonies accompanied by curses that replace the hadd punishment for the husband (for slander) and for the wife (for adultery). The basis is Surah An-Nur 24:6-9, which outlines the procedure when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. The text then clarifies that li'an is only for accusations against one's wife; accusing a non-mahram woman carries the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). If the husband can produce four witnesses, the wife is punished with the hadd of adultery. If she confesses, there is no li'an. The pillar (rukn) of li'an is the four testimonies, so both parties must be qualified to testify (free, adult, sane, Muslim, able to speak). The commentary then lists conditions for li'an: the marriage must be valid (nikah sahih); thus, li'an does not occur in a fasid (invalid) marriage, after a final divorce (bain), or after the wife's death. It does occur in a revocable divorce. Both spouses must be free, mature, sane, Muslim, and capable of speech, and neither should have been previously punished for slander. These conditions are from the Hanafi school as recorded in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'an): Mutual cursing between spouses as prescribed in Quran when husband accuses wife of adultery without witnesses.
القذف (al-qadhf): Accusation of adultery; for non-relative, it carries hadd punishment.
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed punishment for adultery (100 lashes for unmarried, stoning for married) or for false accusation (80 lashes).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of li'an according to this passage?
A) To allow divorce without a reason.
B) To substitute for the hadd punishment when a husband accuses his wife without witnesses.
C) To provide a way for the wife to divorce her husband.
D) To establish the adultery of the wife through testimony.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a Quranically prescribed procedure that substitutes for hadd when a husband accuses his wife without witnesses, provided certain conditions are met.

Definition of Li'an and the Condition of the Wife's Chastity
Defines li'an and explains the condition of the wife's chastity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define li'an in Hanafi fiqh and state the condition of the wife's chastity that triggers the li'an procedure.

Core Idea
Li'an is a multi-step oath-based procedure that replaces the hadd punishment when a husband accuses his chaste wife of adultery without witnesses.

In this passage, the commentator explains the linguistic and legal meaning of li'an, derives its basis from the Quran, and clarifies that it only applies when the wife is 'afifah (chaste). The term 'afifah is deliberately chosen because it is broader than the condition that the accuser be subject to hadd. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining when li'an is valid.

Guided Path
1
Trace the linguistic and legal definition
Look at the commentator's derivation: li'an from la'n (curse). Legally, it is four testimonies with oaths and curses replacing hadd.
Note that it is a substitute, not a punishment.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Read verses 24:6-9; they prescribe the procedure for a husband accusing his wife without witnesses.
This is the primary dalil.
3
Understand the condition of 'afifah
The matn says 'his chaste wife'. The commentator explains that this is deliberately broader than 'the woman for whom her accuser is flogged' because it also includes women who have committed any forbidden intercourse or are under suspicion.
This is a key nuance.
4
List the additional conditions from the commentary
Extract conditions: valid marriage, freedom, puberty, sanity, Islam, speech, no prior hadd for slander, denial by wife, explicit accusation, dar al-Islam.
These conditions ensure li'an is a last resort.

[٢] قوله : زوجته ؛ ذكر في «البحر» وغيره : أن شرطه قيام الزوجية بالنكاح الصحيح، فلا لعان بقذف المنكوحة فاسداً أو المبانة ولو بواحدة ، بخلاف المطلقة رجعية، ولا بقذف زوجته الميتة، ويشترط أيضاً الحرية والبلوغ والعقل والإسلام والنطق وعدم الحدّ في قذف، وهذه شروط راجعة إليهما. [١] قوله : أي عن فعل الزنا غير متهمة به كمن يكون معها ولد ولا يكون له أب معروف ، وإنما اقتصر على كون الزوجة عفيفة، ولم يقل : والمرأة ممن يحد قاذفها، كما قال في «الهداية»، ولا شك أن العفة أعم من كونها ممن يحد قاذفها ؛ لأن اشتراط كونهما من أهل الشهادة ، يدلُّ على الحرية، والتكليف، والإسلام ويشترط في القاذف خاصة عدم إقامة البينة على صدقه، وفي المقذوف خاصة إنكارها وجود الزنا منها وعفتها عنه، ويشترط أيضاً كون القذف بصريح الزنا، وكونه في دار الإسلام
Chapter of Li'an (concerning one who accuses his chaste wife of adultery). [1] His statement: 'Chapter of Li'an'; it (the word li'an) is with a kasra on the lam; it is a verbal noun of la'ana (like qātala) similar to mulā'anah. Its origin is from la'n, which means expulsion and removal from Allah's mercy. Legally, it is an expression of testimonies (shahādāt) emphasized by oaths and coupled with curses, standing in place of the hadd of slander for the husband and the hadd of adultery for the wife; i.e., when they perform li'an, the hadd of slander is dropped from him and the hadd of adultery from her. The proof for it is His statement: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves, then the testimony of one of them is four testimonies by Allah that he is among the truthful, and the fifth is that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars. And it will avert the punishment from her if she testifies four testimonies by Allah that he is among the liars, and the fifth is that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful.' (Quran 24:6-9). These verses indicate that li'an only occurs with the accusation of the wife. As for a foreign woman, accusing her necessitates the hadd, as stated before these verses: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes' (Quran 24:4). And that when witnesses are not produced, if the husband brings four witnesses to her adultery, then there is no li'an and no hadd upon him; rather, she is subjected to the hadd of adultery. Similarly, if she confesses to adultery and confirms the husband. In summary: li'an occurs only when a man accuses his wife of adultery, she denies it, and he does not bring witnesses. And that the pillar (rukn) of li'an is the four testimonies, hence it is required that both be from those eligible for testimony. [2] His statement: 'his wife'; it is mentioned in al-Bahr and others that its condition is the existence of marriage through a valid contract; so there is no li'an with the accusation of a wife in a void marriage (nikāh fāsid) or a divorced woman (mubānah) even with a single divorce, contrary to a revocably divorced woman (muṭallaqa raj'iyyah). Nor does it apply to the accusation of a deceased wife. Also required are freedom, puberty, sanity, Islam, speech, and not having been subjected to hadd for slander. These are conditions that revert to both. [1] His statement: 'i.e., free from the act of adultery, not suspected of it, like one who has a child with no known father. The author restricted to the wife being chaste, and did not say 'and the woman for whom one who accuses her is flogged' as mentioned in al-Hidāyah. There is no doubt that 'chastity' is more general than being one for whom the accuser is flogged, because the condition that both be from the people of testimony indicates freedom, obligation (taklīf), and Islam. It is also required specifically of the accuser that he does not produce evidence for his truthfulness, and specifically of the accused that she denies the occurrence of adultery and her chastity from it. It is also required that the accusation be with explicit words of adultery and that it be in the abode of Islam (dār al-Islam).'
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah is a commentary (sharḥ) on the matn of al-Wiqāyah. It opens the chapter on Li'ān by giving a linguistic and legal definition. Linguistically, li'ān derives from la'n (curse), meaning expulsion from mercy. Legally, it is a set of four testimonies (shahādāt) sworn by each spouse, coupled with a fifth curse or wrath invocation, which replaces the hadd punishment for both: the husband avoids the hadd for false accusation (qadhf), and the wife avoids the hadd for adultery. The author then cites the primary proof from Sūrat al-Nūr (24:6-9), which prescribes this procedure. He explains that li'ān is only for a wife; accusing a foreign woman (non-wife) still requires the standard hadd of eighty lashes for qadhf. Moreover, if the husband produces four witnesses to the wife's adultery, there is no li'ān, and the wife receives the hadd for zinā. Similarly, if the wife confesses, no li'ān. Thus, li'ān is specifically for the scenario where the husband accuses, the wife denies, and he has no witnesses. The commentator then discusses the condition that both spouses must be from 'ahl al-shahādah' (eligible for testimony), which implies freedom, puberty, sanity, Islam, and speech. He elaborates on the condition of the wife's chastity ('iffah): the matn says 'al-'afīfah' (chaste). The commentator notes that the author of al-Wiqāyah deliberately used this word instead of the phrase 'the woman for whom her accuser is flogged' used in al-Hidāyah. The reason is that 'chastity' is more general: it excludes women who are not free from adultery or its suspicion. For example, a woman who has a child with no known father or who has committed any type of forbidden intercourse (even outside zinā, like during menstruation) cannot be the subject of li'ān because her honor is already tainted. Since the condition of being from ahl al-shahādah already implies freedom, obligation, and Islam, mentioning 'chastity' suffices and covers more than the alternative phrasing. Additional conditions mentioned: the accusation must be explicit (by clear words for zinā), the accuser must have no evidence, the accused must deny, and both must be present in dār al-Islām.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'ān): A legal procedure consisting of four testimonies sworn by each spouse, coupled with a fifth curse or wrath, which replaces the hadd punishment for the husband (for false accusation) and the wife (for adultery).
العفيفة (al-'afīfah): A wife who is free from the act of adultery and from any suspicion of it, i.e., she has not committed any forbidden intercourse (including outside of zinā such as during menstruation) and is not under suspicion (e.g., having a child with no known father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for li'an to apply according to this passage?
A) The wife must be Muslim and free
B) The husband must have four witnesses
C) The accusation must be made in dār al-Islām
D) The wife must confess to adultery

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a privileged procedure that only applies when a husband accuses his chaste wife of adultery without witnesses, and the condition of 'chastity' is broader than mere freedom from conviction.

Conditions for Li'an: Wife's Chastity and Witness Qualification
Commentary explaining prerequisites for mutual imprecation (li'an).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for li'an in Hanafi fiqh, explain why the requirement of the wife's chastity is more comprehensive than the Hidayah's phrasing, and apply the condition that both spouses must be qualified witnesses.

Core Idea
Li'an requires the wife to be chaste and both spouses to be fit witnesses; a single unlawful act removes chastity and invalidates li'an.

Li'an is a solemn procedure that saves a husband from the hadd penalty for false accusation and severs the marriage. But not every accusation triggers it. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies two key conditions: the wife must be chaste (afifah), and both spouses must be among those qualified to testify (ahl al-shahada). The commentator explains why specifying chastity is broader and more precise than the phrasing in al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Li'an is a procedure for when a husband accuses his wife of zina or denies paternity. It becomes wajib (obligatory) upon him to avoid the hadd of qadhf if the wife demands it.
The ruling is derived from the requirement to avoid hadd.
2
Understand the condition of chastity
The wife must be 'afifah' – innocent of zina and its accusation. This is broader than 'one whose defamer would be hadded', as it includes women who are not subject to hadd (e.g., non-Muslim, insane, minor) yet are chaste.
Chastity is innocence from any unlawful intercourse, not just zina punishable by hadd.
3
Apply the ahl al-shahada condition
Both spouses must be qualified witnesses: free, Muslim, adult, sane, and not punished for qadhf. This excludes disbelievers, slaves, minors, and those who have been hadded for false accusation.
The sinful (fasiq) and blind are included as they can still testify.
4
Recognize what invalidates the procedure
If the wife has ever committed any unlawful intercourse (e.g., zina, intercourse during menstruation, or via invalid marriage), li'an is not valid because she is not innocent.
Even a single act of prohibited intercourse removes chastity and blocks li'an.
5
Note the procedural trigger
Li'an is initiated by the husband's explicit accusation of zina or implicit denial of paternity, coupled with the wife's demand (since it is her right to clear her name).
If the husband refuses to perform li'an, he is imprisoned until he does so or admits lying (then hadd for qadhf applies).

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the conditions for li'an (mutual imprecation) between spouses. The author explains why the Hidayah only mentions that the wife must be chaste (afifah) rather than 'one whose defamer is hadded.' Chastity is broader: it means innocence from zina and its accusation, which can exist even in a disbeliever, insane woman, or minor, though their defamer is not subject to hadd. The key conditions for li'an are: (1) both spouses must be from ahl al-shahada (qualified witnesses) in terms of freedom, moral responsibility, and Islam; (2) the husband accuses explicitly of zina or implicitly by denying paternity; (3) the wife demands the consequence; (4) the wife is chaste (i.e., never knowingly committed unlawful intercourse). If the wife has engaged in any form of unlawful intercourse (even via invalid marriage, a single instance of zina, or intercourse during menstruation), li'an is not valid because she is not innocent. The commentary also clarifies that if the husband refuses li'an, he is imprisoned until he either performs it or admits lying (then he is subject to hadd for qadhf). The demand is required because the wife's right to defend her honor triggers the process. In case of paternity denial, the husband's own demand is needed to remove the child from his lineage.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li‘ān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when husband accuses wife of zina or denies paternity, involving oaths of condemnation and invocation of curse.
عفيفة (‘afīfah): A woman innocent of zina and its accusation, i.e., never knowingly committed unlawful intercourse.
أهل الشهادة (ahl al-shahādah): Those qualified to bear testimony in a Shari'ah court: free, Muslim, adult, sane, and not convicted of qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because she cannot be a witness.
D) Because the husband must be truthful.

Key Takeaway
Li'an requires the wife to be chaste and both spouses to be qualified witnesses; any prior unlawful intercourse by the wife invalidates the procedure.

When Li'an Is Not Required: The Ahliyyat al-Shahada Condition
Explains when li'an is not required due to disqualifying statuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the circumstances in which li'an (mutual imprecation) is not required and determine when the hadd penalty for qadhf applies.

Core Idea
Li'an requires both spouses to have legal capacity to testify; otherwise it drops.

In the Hanafi school, li'an is a solemn procedure used when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. But it is not always available. This lesson explores a key condition: both spouses must possess ahliyyat al-shahada (qualification to give testimony). When one or both lack it due to slavery, disbelief, prior qadhf punishment, or minor/insanity, the li'an obligation and the hadd penalty for false accusation are affected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Li'an is wajib on a husband when he accuses his wife of zina without witnesses, provided conditions are met.
2
Identify the condition for li'an
Both spouses must have ahliyyat al-shahada: being free, Muslim, adult, sane, and not previously punished for qadhf.
3
List disqualifying statuses for the husband
The husband is disqualified if he is a slave, a disbeliever, or has been punished for qadhf (hadd).
4
List disqualifying statuses for the wife
The wife is disqualified if she is a slave, a disbeliever, punished for qadhf, a minor, insane, or a known adulteress.
5
Apply the principle to determine hadd and li'an
If li'an drops due to a reason from one side (e.g., husband disqualified) and the qadhf is valid, hadd is imposed on the wife (for zina); if qadhf is invalid, no hadd and no li'an. If it drops from both sides or from the wife's side alone (with valid qadhf), no hadd and no li'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لاعن لاعنت، وإلا حُبِسَت حتّى تلاعنَ أو تُصَدِّقَه: فينفي نسب ولدها عنه، لكن لا يجب عليها الحد بهذا التصديق. فإن كان هو عبداً، أو كافراً، أو محدوداً في قذف حدّ. وإن صلح هو شاهداً، وهي أمة، أو كافرة، أو محدودة في قذف، أو صبية، أو مجنونة، أو زانية فلا حد عليه، ولا لعان لأنه ليس من أهل اللعان؛ لعدم أهلية الشهادة. والأصل فيه على ما في البحر والمنح وغيرهما: إن اللعان إذا سقط لمعنى من جهة بأن لم يصلح شاهداً لرقه أو كفره، فلو كان القذف صحيحاً حد، وإلا فلا حد ولا لعان. وأما لو سقط لمعنى من جهتهما فلا حد ولا لعان، ولو سقط من جهتهما كما لو كانا محدودين في قذف فهو كالأول.
If he performs li'an, she must perform li'an; otherwise she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms him: thereby the lineage of her child from him is negated, but she does not incur the hadd by this confirmation. If he is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf with hadd. And if he is fit to be a witness, while she is a slave, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf, or a minor, or insane, or an adulteress, then there is no hadd upon him and no li'an, because she is not of the people of li'an due to lack of qualification for testimony. The principle according to what is in al-Bahr, al-Minh, and others: li'an drops due to a reason from one side, such as when one is not fit to be a witness due to slavery or disbelief; then if the qadhf was valid, hadd is applied, otherwise no hadd and no li'an. As for when it drops due to a reason from both sides, then no hadd and no li'an. If it drops from both sides, as when both are those who have been punished for qadhf, it is like the first.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah explains the conditions under which li'an (mutual imprecation) is not required. The core principle is that li'an is only valid when both spouses possess ahliyyat al-shahada (capacity to testify). If the husband is a slave, disbeliever, or has been punished for qadhf (false accusation of zina), he lacks this capacity. Similarly, if the wife is a slave, disbeliever, previously punished for qadhf, minor, insane, or known to be an adulteress, she also lacks capacity. In such cases, the husband does not perform li'an and does not incur the hadd penalty for qadhf, unless his accusation was valid (i.e., she actually committed zina) and the impediment is only on his side. If both lack capacity, no hadd and no li'an are imposed. The author supports this with references to earlier Hanafi works like al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Minh.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses, involving oaths and curses.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a chaste person; a hudud crime punishable by 80 lashes.
أهلية الشهادة (ahliyyat al-shahada): Legal capacity to testify in court; requires freedom, Islam, adulthood, sanity, and integrity ('adalah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband must perform li'an and incurs hadd.
B) The husband does not perform li'an and incurs hadd.
C) The husband does not perform li'an and does not incur hadd.
D) The husband must perform li'an but does not incur hadd.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is not required when a spouse lacks legal capacity to testify, which also affects the hadd penalty for qadhf.

Conditions for Li'an and Hadd When Wife Lacks Testimony Eligibility
Ruling on absence of hadd and li'an when wife lacks shahadah eligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which li'an and hadd are waived in Hanafi law and apply the hadith proof to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
Li'an requires mutual eligibility for testimony; if the wife lacks it, no li'an and no hadd on the husband.

In this passage, the author addresses a specific scenario: a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses. Normally, he would face hadd qadhf or perform li'an. However, if the wife is not a valid witness (due to slavery, disbelief, flogging for slander, minority, insanity, or her own adultery), the husband avoids both hadd and li'an. This lesson unpacks the conditions that trigger this exception, the underlying principle, and the hadith evidence from Ibn Majah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the consequence when the husband is a valid witness but the wife is not: no hadd on him and no li'an.
The ruling is derived from the hadith of four women.
2
List the wife's disqualifying traits
Enumerate the six conditions mentioned: slavery, disbelief, flogging for slander, minority, insanity, and being an adulteress.
Each trait removes her eligibility for shahadah.
3
Apply the principle of causal attribution
If li'an falls due to a reason on her side (her disqualification), no hadd; if it falls due to a reason on both sides, also no hadd; if the accusation was valid (she truly is unchaste), no hadd.
The principle is from Al-Bahr and Al-Munah.
4
Describe the surah of li'an
Recognize the wording: four oaths of truthfulness and a fifth imprecation of curse.
This surah is the prescribed form for li'an in the Hanafi school.
5
Confirm with the hadith
Cite the hadith listing four women with whom li'an is not performed, showing the common element of testimony eligibility.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but sufficient for deriving the rule.
